LU-2525 ldlm: add asynchronous flocks

Add support of asynchronous flocks.
They are used only by Linux nfsd for now.

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2015-07-13 14:45:07.000000000) ---
Patch Set 23: Code-Review-1

Also, as this is currently, it needs a compat flag.  Clients without this code will crash when a waiting lock is unlocked by the server.  (That waiting lock is granted with mode 0 without the 'FAILED' flag set - This code destroys the lock in that case, but for clients without it, it leads to actually granting the lock (with mode 0) rather than destroying it, and eventually to a crash when that lock is destroyed.)

--- Message (Fan Yong, 2016-08-31 08:22:37.000000000) ---
Patch Set 35: Code-Review-1

(8 comments)

In addition to the reordered lock-unlock RPC issue, there are some other small issues to be considered as the comment.

--- Message (Vitaly Fertman, 2016-09-05 21:31:35.000000000) ---
Patch Set 35:

(5 comments)

--- Message (Vitaly Fertman, 2016-09-05 23:58:07.000000000) ---
Patch Set 35:

"Then why not make Lustre to self-sponsor FA_FL_CANCELED internally when F_UNLCK. Then even if the upper later user (VFS) miss to call vfs_cancel_lock() before unlock, Lustre itself still can guarantee to be in healthy status."

it works fine with the current interface and it is not going to change soon, we have checked the latest kernels and there are no symptoms of that. thus, we should think about this idea just as about a possible future probability and not practical so far.

having said it, I do not think it is worth to do any kind of changes in the main logic, Lustre have other cases of such dependancies and never tried to be 'self-sponsored' doing everything at the 1st step (e.g. lookup + open).

I do not even say flocks is one of the topics for a complete re-design. which probability is higher, new flocks or changed interface? :)

at the same time, I agree it would be not bad to create a test to check it still works fine with future kernels. however having just a future probability issue and such a large change taking a lot of resources to keep it in sync with the current master code, I would say it depends very much on how much time such a test will take to implement.

--- Message (Vitaly Fertman, 2016-09-06 00:26:02.000000000) ---
Patch Set 34:

(4 comments)

--- Message (Oleg Drokin, 2016-09-06 00:34:15.000000000) ---
Patch Set 35:

I am also of the opinion that we are to adhere to the in-kernel API, if the API in the kernel is changed - then we will need to face it once adjusting, otherwise we are spending tons of resources for a "what if" problem that might never materialize.

--- Message (Fan Yong, 2016-09-06 06:46:33.000000000) ---
Patch Set 35:

>  do not even say flocks is one of the topics for a complete re-design. which probability is higher, new flocks or changed interface? :)
at the same time, I agree it would be not bad to create a test to check it still works fine with future kernels. however having just a future probability issue and such a large change taking a lot of resources to keep it in sync with the current master code, I would say it depends very much on how much time such a test will take to implement.

I will NOT suggest to enhance current logic to handle future possible kernel changes. What I want to express is that Lustre should try the best to make things to be self-controble. In this case, we can avoid the re-ordered async flock lock and unlock RPC issue.

Currently, it seems that the NFSD is the unique user for async flock, and it follows its own rules to resolve such trouble. But Lustre exports the lock API to VFS, we cannot forbid other kernel developers to use that. As for whether they will follow NFSD's used rules, that is out of control unless there is official document for that. That is risk.

There is another exception, the kernel cleanup routine for thread exit abnormally, Under such case, kernel will directly unlock all the locks attached to the files that are opened by the exiting thread, in spite of whether related RPCs have been handled the the MDT or not.

So handling such trouble inside Lustre is the more safe. It is not for future kernels. The patch http://review.whamcloud.com/#/c/22247/ is one possible solution. It bases on the current patch, and not complex. You also can investigate other solutions or modify such patch directly.

--- Message (Vitaly Fertman, 2016-09-06 12:21:09.000000000) ---
Patch Set 35:

> Currently, it seems that the NFSD is the unique user for async flock, and it follows its own rules to resolve such trouble. But Lustre exports the lock API to VFS, we cannot forbid other kernel developers to use that. As for whether they will follow NFSD's used rules, that is out of control unless there is official document for that. That is risk.


the semantics is already clearly stated in the kernel:

 /**
 * vfs_cancel_lock - file byte range unblock lock
 * @filp: The file to apply the unblock to
 * @fl: The lock to be unblocked
 *
 * Used by lock managers to cancel blocked requests
 */
 int vfs_cancel_lock(struct file *filp, struct file_lock *fl)
 {
        if (filp->f_op && filp->f_op->lock)
                return filp->f_op->lock(filp, F_CANCELLK, fl);
        return 0;
 }

 EXPORT_SYMBOL_GPL(vfs_cancel_lock);

- the exported method for cancelling blocked pending requests, and all the callers must use this api.

> There is another exception, the kernel cleanup routine for thread exit abnormally, Under such case, kernel will directly unlock all the locks attached to the files that are opened by the exiting thread, in spite of whether related RPCs have been handled the the MDT or not.

this is not a risk at all, because only sync locks are exported and only those are closed. having started with async flocks, one is supposed to start using that api showed above.

--- Message (Vitaly Fertman, 2016-09-06 20:02:42.000000000) ---
Patch Set 35:

having said this, let's clarify the current semantics:
F_CANCELLK cancels blocked pending requests, but not locks, i.e. granted locks are not supposed to be cancelled at all;
F_SETLK type=F_UNLCK cancels existing locks.

and it is probably better to cleanup it in an opposite way to minimise the amount of RPCs - to not send any unlock on F_CANCELLK at all, but only to mark pending locks with FA_FL_CANCELED and exist. meaning, a later reply for such a lock will issue an unlock.

at the same time, your suspicions in this part of the code were right, after reviewing it once again I found a case when it is possible to not get the server lock unlocked. will be fixed in the next patch version.

--- Message (Oleg Drokin, 2016-09-12 04:03:23.000000000) ---
Patch Set 35:

(6 comments)

I guess the idea to simpify cancellk handling by just marking the request somehow and once the reply is received - cancel the now unneeded lock is not too bad.

There are two cases here actually:
1. the enqueue is in flight - we need to mark the request and that's it, then act on it once the reply is received.
2. enqueue hasfinished, but he lock was blocked and is now in waiting list. In this case it's ok to just kill the lock locally and then CP ast would get ESTALE of some sort and server will cancel the lock.
We can also send a courtesy lock cancel on this waiting lock (need to ensure it actually works with flocks) to the server so that if we win this race, server does not do any xtra granting on it at all.

I am also not super fond of another list - the enqueueing one, but I guess there were not any easy options left?
For example struct file_lock has fl_u union that holds "afs" nfs sturcture, this is for filesystems like lustre (and nfs client) -so we are free to use it. We cannot really patch the kernel of course, but we can create our own structure and jsut cast f_u to that (make sure it's not bigger than nfs one) and then we can do all sort of cool things like link to requests that are still in flight there and then we can get rid of this ugly enqueuing list and perhaps some other kludges.

Another annoyance, with this patch, running connectathon lock tests, a spurios mssage is generated that needs to be silenced:
[ 2929.225521] LustreError: 11-0: lustre-MDT0000-mdc-ffff880091957800: operation ldlm_enqueue to node 0@lo failed: rc = -11
